"Ugh, not again," you spout as the old wagon shutters, then dies. Stranded on the road again, but this time, your money has gone dry. All but your 50 dollar bill that Grandma gave you on her last Christmas. You've been saving it for when you needed it most, but surely, it won't be enough.

The door creaks open, and you step out into the night sky, coughing up the smoke from your fried vehicle. After pushing your car off the road and between the trees, there isn't much else left for you to do, so you begin to wander down the dark, lonely street.

But at the end of the road, where concrete turned to stone turned to dirt, you notice a light up ahead, on the top of a hill. 

As you waltz into the old, wooden shack, your eyes begin to light up with the fire of a thousand suns. Roulette wheels! Poker tables! And in a dark corner of the abandoned casino, sits a dealer, shuffling cards for a new round of Blackjack. That 50 dollars might just come in handy after all. Thanks, Grandma!

As you go to sit down at the table, you hear the Dealer cough, then watch as he sits up.

In a deep, and yet strained voice, the Dealer, cloaked in darkness, poses a question to you.

Would you like to play a game of Blackjack? You have $50

Victory! Small, fragile, temporary. But yours.

Dealer secures Blackjack! Game over for you, loser!

Your new balance is $56 - $7 = $49

After playing a few rounds of Blackjack, the dealer points to the door. Without questioning his word, and with your winnings in hand, you scurry to the door, eager to get some sleep after such a long day. Making it back to your car, ditched on the side of the road, but no longer engulfed in smoke, you lay down, and close your eyes. It's time to rest.

══════════ ~ ~ ~ Morning, Day 4 ~ ~ ~ ══════════
The warm feeling in your gut fades. Beginner's Luck has worn off.

The man sees you, and walks up to you.

"You. You're awake. Good. You know that you aren't supposed to be here? ""This isn't a spot for people to live. This is a road for people to drive. I hope you know this."

"Do you know this?" "You don't know this? How don't you know this? It's super obvious stuff, man. ""People don't live at places where they're not supposed to, and that's exactly what you're doing right now. ""I'd suggest you stop it, right this instant."

After the man tells you this, he looks up, and stares at the sun. And after about 20 seconds, he rubs his eyes, walks back to his car, and drives off.

The temperature is perfect. Not too hot, not too cold. The car seat cradles you like it was designed for sleeping.

It wasn't. But tonight, everything conspires to give you rest. The parking lot is quiet. No sirens. No drunks. No existential dread.

You sleep like a baby. A baby who lives in a car, but a well-rested baby nonetheless.

Sleep won't come. You try counting sheep. The sheep turn into cards. The cards turn into debts. The debts turn into a math problem you already know the answer to but keep solving anyway, hoping the answer changes.

You lie there, eyes open, listening to your own breathing and the distant hum of a highway that exists for people going somewhere. Somewhere out there, people are sleeping in actual beds, in actual houses, with mortgages that embarrass them and futures they take for granted.

You wonder if they know. How lucky the ordinary is. How you'd give everything you're chasing just to feel that ordinary again. Probably not. Nobody ever knows until it's already gone and they're lying in a car in the dark making deals with the ceiling.

══════════ ~ ~ ~ Morning, Day 6 ~ ~ ~ ══════════

A man with a shotgun. Ski mask. Shaking hands. This is really happening.

The robber swings the gun around, wild-eyed.



You duck behind a shelf. Slowly, carefully, you crawl toward the back.

The robber is focused on the register. You're almost to the storage room...

A chip bag crinkles under your knee. The robber spins.

"I SEE YOU! GET OUT HERE!"

The shotgun is pointed right at you. You raise your hands and step out.

"Think you're smart? Think you can hide from me?"

He hits you with the stock. Your vision explodes into stars.



Sitting in your car, your mind drifts. You dream of water. Dark water. Deep water. Rising water.

You're in a car—your car—and water is pouring in through every crack.

You can't open the doors. The pressure is too much. The windows won't break.

The water reaches your waist. Your chest. Your neck. Your mouth.

You scream but water fills your lungs instead of air.

...

You wake up GASPING. Clawing at your throat. Soaking wet with sweat.

Just a dream. Just a dream. Just a—

Your feet are wet. You look down.

Rain. It's raining. Water leaked through a crack in your window.

Just rain. You're fine. You're fine. You're fine.
Your mind feels... foggy. Something isn't right.

══════════ ~ ~ ~ Morning, Day 8 ~ ~ ~ ══════════
You slept like a baby. A big, grown baby in a car, but a baby nonetheless.

You're looking for a dropped quarter under the driver's seat when your hand touches something cold and hard. Metal.
You pull it out. It's a lockbox. A real, proper lockbox. Steel. Heavy. About the size of a shoebox. There's a keyhole on the front and a combination dial on top.
It's padlocked shut with a serious-looking Master lock.
You shake it. Something slides around inside. Multiple somethings. They clink against each other like glass or metal.
This wasn't here yesterday. You'd have noticed. Which means someone put it in your car while you were sleeping.
On the bottom, scratched into the metal with something sharp:
"DON'T OPEN UNTIL READY"
Probably wise. You don't know what's in there. Could be valuables. Could be evidence. Could be somebody's ashes.
Could be a lot of things.
You put the lockbox in your trunk. You need to find whoever left it — or at least find the key.

══════════ ~ ~ ~ Morning, Day 12 ~ ~ ~ ══════════
The sun hits your face through the windshield and you don't even mind. That's how good you feel.

Your eyes open. At least, you think they do.
Your eyes are open. You can see the ceiling of your car. The streetlight outside casting its orange glow. Everything is normal.
Except you can't move.
Not paralyzed-numb. Paralyzed-trapped. Your body is awake but it won't listen. Your arms are dead weight. Your legs won't respond. You can't even turn your head.
Then you see it. In the corner of your vision. Something in the back seat.
A shape. Darker than dark. It doesn't have edges — it has suggestions of edges. Like smoke that decided to sit down.
It's watching you. You can feel it watching you even though it doesn't have eyes.
Your breathing gets faster. Your heart is hammering. But you. Can't. Move.
The shape leans forward. Closer. You can feel cold radiating off it like an open freezer.
Then — snap — your body releases. You bolt upright, gasping. The back seat is empty. Nothing there. Just the dark.
You don't sleep for the rest of the night. You sit with every light on and your eyes open, watching the back seat in the rearview mirror.
Nothing comes. But the cold lingers.

Your current sanity: 43%

The trees outside your car window are too still. Unnaturally still.
A fat raccoon waddles up to your car and sits on the hood. It stares at you through the windshield with beady, knowing eyes.

Then, impossibly, it speaks.

"Hey. You. Yeah, you. The gambler living in a car."

You blink. The raccoon continues.

"Look, I eat garbage for a living. GARBAGE. And you know what? I'm happy. You know why?"

You shake your head, dumbfounded.

"Because I don't compare myself to other raccoons. I just do my thing. Eat trash. Wash my hands. Live my life."

"You? You're out here chasing a million dollars. That's YOUR garbage. And that's beautiful, man."

The raccoon stands up, brushes off its fur, and waddles away.

"Go get that garbage, champ!"

You... you feel strangely inspired.
A sense of clarity washes over you. The fog lifts, if only a little.

Without a word (obviously), the mime begins to act out a scene. He's pretending to be trapped in a box. Classic.

Then he mimes... crying? Counting money? Losing at cards?

Wait. Is he acting out YOUR life?

The mime finishes with a dramatic death scene, tongue out and everything, then springs back up and takes a bow.

The mime looks devastated. He mimes a single tear rolling down his cheek, then slowly backs away, never breaking eye contact.

You feel kind of bad about that.




Your current sanity: 59%
You can't sleep, so you walk. The city is different at this hour — quieter, more honest, the neon signs humming a frequency that only works on insomniacs and people with nothing left to protect.

You pass closed shops and sleeping houses. Everyone behind those walls has a bed. A fridge. A door that locks from the inside. You walk past all of it without slowing down, because the rhythm is the only thing that works — step, step, step, forward, one direction, don't stop.

When you get back to your car, you're tired in the right way for once. The kind of tired that actually leads to sleep.

The pressure on your chest increases. It's hard to breathe. The shadow is heavy. Heavier than anything physical.
"All you have to do is say yes."

Your body snaps free again. You sit up, drenched in sweat. The car is empty. Warm. Normal.

Wait, is he doing Jameson? He's pretending to ride a horse. That's definitely Jameson.
Oh no. He's straightening an invisible tie. That's the red suit guy. Phil. He nails the judgmental stare.
The mime finishes with a new bit: he pulls an invisible rope and lifts himself off the ground, dangling in the air. Then he falls, catches himself, and takes a bow.
He's sweating under the face paint. This guy takes his craft seriously.
The mime beams. He reaches behind your ear and produces a very real, very shiny quarter.

"Dear stranger,"

"I was where you are three years ago. Same parking lot. Same car seat. Same view of the same ceiling. I played cards too — not blackjack, poker — but the principle is the same. Gambling to survive. Surviving to gamble."
"Someone helped me. I never found out who. They left me money and a chance and a note that said 'Pass it on.'"
"So I'm passing it on."
"The keys are to an apartment. Studio, nothing fancy. Rent is paid through the end of the month. After that, it's up to you. The address is on the keychain."
"I know what you're thinking. Is this real? Is this a trap? Who does this?"
"People who remember."
"The photograph was just to prove I could have hurt you. I didn't. I won't. I'm just someone who was you, once."
"Good luck. And when you can — pass it on."
It's unsigned.
You sit in your car holding a letter from a stranger who was you three years ago, and you cry. Not because you're sad. Because someone remembered what it felt like and did something about it.
The address on the keychain leads to a building on the west side. Third floor. Unit 3B. The key fits.
Inside: a studio apartment. Clean. Small. A bed, a kitchenette, a bathroom with hot water. A window that faces east — morning sun.
On the kitchen counter, one more note:
"The fridge has groceries. The bed has clean sheets. Welcome home — for now."
It's the nicest room you've been in since everything went wrong.
You sit on the bed. You take off your shoes. You look at the ceiling, which is not the ceiling of your car.
It's different up here.You fold the letter and put it in your pocket. Maybe one day you'll pass it on too.
Whiskers stretches — front paws out, butt in the air, back arched. The morning yoga routine.
Having Whiskers by your side makes the world a little less cruel.
You can't sleep, so you walk. The city is different at this hour — quieter, more honest, the neon signs humming a frequency that only works on insomniacs and people with nothing left to protect.

You pass closed shops and sleeping houses. Everyone behind those walls has a bed. A fridge. A door that locks from the inside. You walk past all of it without slowing down, because the rhythm is the only thing that works — step, step, step, forward, one direction, don't stop.

When you get back to your car, you're tired in the right way for once. The kind of tired that actually leads to sleep.



As the sun begins to set, and the stars light up in the night sky, you walk to the casino, eager to play more Blackjack. 
Back for more? The cards appreciate your persistence.

Here's a quote my dad used to say: "Let's embark on a journey, a meandering path not unlike the serpentine wanderings of a leaf caught in a capricious autumn breeze, which, as it dances to the silent music of nature, reminds us of the unpredictable choreography of existence. This leaf, let's call it Gerald, flutters with an elegance borne of happenstance, a fragile vessel for the whims of the wind. Gerald's journey is not linear, nor is it bound by the rigid expectations of society's ceaselessly grinding gears. Instead, Gerald twirls, dips, and soars, embracing the chaos with a grace we can only aspire to. Now, consider the ant, industrious and steadfast, a creature of purpose and communal toil. Our ant, whom we'll name Beatrice, marches diligently on her quest for sustenance, her life a testament to the virtues of hard work and persistence. Yet, in the grand tapestry of the cosmos, what is Beatrice but a speck, a mere blip on the infinite canvas of the universe? And yet, does her insignificance in the face of the vast unknown render her efforts moot? I posit that it does not, for in the grand scheme, all actions, large and small, contribute to the intricate mosaic of existence. But back to Gerald, who by now has traversed the convoluted landscapes of our imagination, touching upon the existential questions that haunt the periphery of our consciousness. What can we learn from Gerald and Beatrice? Is it their resilience, their unyielding will to persist in the face of the insurmountable odds stacked against them by the very nature of their existence? Or is it, perhaps, the simple beauty of their dance, a reminder that life, in all its complexity and confusion, offers moments of sublime beauty, fleeting and precious, to be cherished and remembered? As Gerald finally comes to rest upon the earth, joining Beatrice in the eternal cycle of life and death, we are reminded that all journeys, whether they be of leaves or ants or the human heart, are interconnected in the grand, bewildering dance of the cosmos. So, what was the point of this story, you may ask? Well, that, my friend, is entirely up to you."


══════════ ~ ~ ~ Morning, Day 37 ~ ~ ~ ══════════
You slept so hard you forgot where you were for a second. That's the good kind of confusion.

A glossy black limousine is quietly approaching your wagon. As you sit up from your slumber, you read 'Oswald's Optimal Outoparts' cursively engraved in gold letters on the side of the limo. Waving the vehicle down, the limo slows, then stops before you. The door opens vertically, and a large red carpet is rolled out onto the street. You watch in awe as a man, with a combover and a tuxedo, walks out before you. He coughs, then speaks.
"Why hello there! The name's Oswald, as you can see by my nametag. Do you like my bowtie? Well of course you do! It appears your limousine has broken down." Oswald pulls a gold whistle out of his pocket, and blows into it deeply. "Oh Stuart!" You watch as a bald man in a tailcoat suit, no taller than 4 feet, hobbles over to Oswald's side.
"This is Stuart! He will fix your limousine up for a fair price. Let's say, I don't know, I suppose a fair price is 500,000 dollars. Okay, the look on your face says that I'm making a big mistake. Let's try $850, and Stuart here will get you back on the road! Do you accept?" 
"Jolly good! Stuart!" You watch as the little man walks to the front of your wagon, opens the hood, and jumps in. You can't really see what's going on, but after a couple of minutes, Stuart jumps back out, covered in oil.
Your new balance is $2,089 - $850 = $1,239
Your car has been fixed! You can now drive around!
"Oh my Stuart! Someone got a little too excited, didn't you? Yep, you're getting a bath as soon as we get back to the shop. Thanks again, stranger, it's been a pleasure doing business with you. I recall it's good custom to tip after events like this, yes? Here, take this." Oswald hands you a bright green bill, worth $50.
Your new balance is $1,239 + $50 = $1,289
And with that, you watch as Stuart rolls up the red carpet. Oswald and Stuart get back in the limo, and drive off into the distance.
Whiskers sits with her back to you. The cold shoulder is real.

After wandering from your vehicle, you find yourself deep in the woods. Squirrels run by and up into the trees. The sun hits every branch and casts a shadow below. And you wander on a natural path, journeying into the unknown.

As you walk along the path, you notice someone leaning against a tree in front of you. As you get closer, you notice that the person's face is blue, their eyes are bloodshot, and they don't appear to be breathing.

You begin to panic, before thinking through the situation. They're already dead, so there's nothing you can do to help them. Maybe they had some money on them? I mean, they're not gonna use it. Why shouldn't you?

══════════ ~ ~ ~ Morning, Day 43 ~ ~ ~ ══════════
You yawn, stretch, and feel genuinely alive. Not just surviving. Actually alive.

A sharp knock on your window. You look up to see a gaunt man in a stained trench coat peering at you through the glass. His teeth are yellow, his eyes are bloodshot, and he's holding a pocket watch that looks far too expensive for someone dressed like him.

You roll down the window just a crack.

"Nice pile of cash you got there," he rasps, nodding at the money in your passenger seat. "You look like a collector. A finder of rare things."

He glances around nervously, then leans closer.

"Name's Gus. Grimy Gus, they call me. Got a little shop down on Fifth and Nowhere. ""If you ever find yourself with... unusual items... things that don't belong in the light of day... I can make them disappear. For a fair price."

He taps his nose conspiratorially.

"Collectibles, trinkets, treasures. Things you picked up on your... adventures. I don't ask questions. Just cash on the barrel."

He hands you a grimy business card through the crack in the window. It reads: "Grimy Gus's Pawn Emporium - We Buy What Others Won't"

"Come by sometime. You won't regret it. Probably."

He shuffles off into the morning mist before you can respond.

A new shop has been unlocked: Grimy Gus's Pawn Emporium

=== CAR TROUBLE ===
You turn the key. The engine tries to catch but fails. Again and again.

It's not the battery - you can hear it trying. Something else is wrong.

You have no tools, no knowledge. Just frustration.

You call for help. The afternoon evaporates waiting for a mechanic.



A sleek black limousine glides to a stop. The door opens vertically. Oswald steps out.
"My goodness. I was simply passing through when I recognized my handiwork. What a small world."
He produces a leather-bound toolkit from inside the limo and gets straight to work.
"A professional rate for a repeat customer — "$200". Shall we?"
Accept Oswald's roadside repair for $200? 

Your new balance is $2,250 - $200 = $2,050
"Splendid. Good as new. I do insist on quality. And do allow me —"

Your new balance is $2,050 + $50 = $2,100
Oswald presses $50 into your hand.
He packs his kit, adjusts his bowtie, and the limo glides away. Afternoon saved.

══════════ ~ ~ ~ Morning, Day 51 ~ ~ ~ ══════════
Your body feels like it got a factory reset overnight. Joints? Smooth. Back? Fine. Mood? Immaculate.

You've been fighting sleep for days. Coffee. Slapping yourself. Driving with the windows down.
It doesn't matter. It comes when it wants to.
This time, you don't even realize you've fallen asleep. One moment you're driving. The next, you're parked somewhere you don't recognize, engine off, and you can't move.
The shadow fills the entire car. It's everywhere. In the mirrors, in the corners, in the gaps between the seats.
"I'm not what you think I am."

"I'm not a monster. I'm a door. Walk through me and the pain stops. The cold stops. The hunger, the loneliness, the endless, stupid cards — all of it. Gone."

"I've been watching you lose for so long. I'm offering you the only guaranteed win."

The cold is so intense your teeth are chattering. Or trying to — your jaw is locked.
Inside your head, you hear the question clearly:
"Do you accept?"

No.
Not a thought. A word. Your lips move even though your body is frozen. You force it out through locked teeth and a locked jaw.
"No."
The shadow recoils. The cold retreats. For the first time, you hear something from it that isn't confidence.
"...Interesting."

Your body releases. You sit up. The car is normal. Warm. Silent.
But in the rearview mirror, just for a second, you see it retreat into the shadows behind your headrest. And you could swear it's smiling.
Whiskers paws at your face until you open your eyes. Then she walks away. She just wanted to know you were alive.
Having Whiskers by your side makes the world a little less cruel.

Before you can react, the mime hears something. He snaps his head to the left, drops the signs, and sprints away faster than any mime should be able to run.
You pick up the signs. On the back of the last one, in small handwriting:
"My name is Gerald. If they find out I told you, I'm done. -G"

══════════ ~ ~ ~ Morning, Day 59 ~ ~ ~ ══════════

Same clothes. Same face. Same confused expression.

You blink. Your double blinks.

You take a step forward. It takes a step forward.

You wave. It waves.

And then it smiles-a smile you've never made, too wide, too knowing-and walks behind a van.

You run over. Nothing. No one. Just empty parking spaces.

You stand there for a long time, heart pounding, wondering if you're finally losing your mind.

Maybe you are.

That's the mime. That's Gerald.
You walk over. He sees you coming and tenses up, like he might run.
"Please. Sit down. Don't make it obvious."
His voice is quiet. Raspy. Like he hasn't used it in a long time.
"I was a performer. A real one. Theaters, festivals, the whole thing. ""Then I saw something I shouldn't have. Backstage at a casino. Money changing hands. ""Important hands. The kind of hands that make people disappear."
"The mime thing started as a disguise. Turns out, nobody looks twice at a mime. ""You're invisible. The perfect hiding spot is where everyone can see you."
He glances around nervously.
"I've been watching you because you're in their territory. The gambling road. ""They don't like people winning too much. Drawing attention."
Gerald nods approvingly.
"Smart. The less you know, the safer you are. Just... be careful."
He walks away. No moonwalk this time. Just a scared man in a brown jacket.

══════════ ~ ~ ~ Morning, Day 66 ~ ~ ~ ══════════
That was some quality sleep. Five stars. Would sleep again.

Before dealing, the Dealer reaches into his vest pocket and places the photograph face-up on the table between you. The woman. The girl. The yellow house.
"Her name was Maria. Our daughter was Sofia."
He says it like pulling a splinter — quick, to minimize the pain.
"I was a math teacher. Can you believe that? ""I taught probability and statistics at a high school in Riverside. ""I was good at it. The kids liked me. I made math jokes. ""You know how hard it is to make a math joke land?"
A smile flickers across his face. Ghost of a life.
"Maria was a nurse. Sofia wanted to be a veterinarian. She loved animals. ""Every stray cat in the neighborhood ended up on our porch."
His voice goes flat. The next part costs him everything.
"Car accident. Both of them. I was at the school grading papers when I got the call. ""The hospital Maria worked at was the one they were taken to. ""Her own colleagues..."
He can't finish that sentence. He doesn't need to.
"I left everything. The house, the job, the life. Started driving. ""I knew cards — I'd been running poker night for the faculty for years. ""Turns out, when you understand probability, you make a decent dealer."
"This road. Your car. These cards. It's all I have left. ""And the photo. I keep the photo."
He picks up the photograph and holds it for a moment before putting it back.
"You asked. So now you know. Does it change anything?"
"...Yeah. It does."
The Dealer nods. Maybe that's enough.
He deals the next hand. The cards feel different in his hands. Lighter.
Whiskers demands breakfast by walking across your face. Repeatedly.
Having Whiskers by your side makes the world a little less cruel.

A small boat drifts out of the fog - a pirogue, poled by a figure in a hooded cloak. The witch of the swamp. She stops next to you, looking down with eyes that have seen too much.

"You're far from shore, child. Looking for something?"

She pulls you into her boat and poles you to shore. As you climb out, she hands you something - a small bundle of herbs tied with red string.

"For protection. You'll need it."

══════════ ~ ~ ~ Morning, Day 68 ~ ~ ~ ══════════
You actually want to get out of the car. This is a historic moment.

Through the windshield-again-a car is parked right in front of you. You can feel your blood start to boil. What's this guy's problem? As you open the door and get out of your car, you notice the man in his bright red suit, once again peering into your trunk.

The man sees you, and walks up to you, with a pistol holstered to his waist.

"You. I'm done playing around. It's time to move. I mean it." You look down at the gun on his waist. It looks fancy, and certainly deadly.

"I wouldn't test me if I were you. It's time to go, now."

"Will you leave?" "That's great. Fantastic. But I don't believe a word that comes out of your filthy mouth. Prove it. Leave. Go away. GET OUT."

You are fueled with anger. Who is this guy, and what gives him the right to harass you? All for being homeless? No longer. You reach for the gun on his waist.

You snatch the gun from his holster, and he tackles you to the ground. You fight and struggle, each of you with both hands on the pistol. In the distance, you hear the horn of a freight truck beginning to drive closer. The man punches you in the arm, and it stings. Without thinking twice, you give the man a headbutt, and he falls backwards into the road. You point the gun at the man, and he begins to cry.

"Please, I'm sorry. I didn't mean to cause any of this. ""I just, I hate seeing people living on the streets, all alone. ""I was just trying to help you. Just, please, for the love of god, don't hurt me."

As the man begs for his life, the freight truck continues to draw closer, and the horn gets louder. You point at the truck in the distance, but the man can't see through the tears in his eyes.

"Please, I have a family. I have children. My name is Phil. I don't wanna die. I'm too young. I can't die. I can't die. I ca-" You watch as the freight truck crushes Phil, and continues down the road. Nothing remained but the splotches of blood that splattered the road where he once stood.

After sitting a while, and recollecting your thoughts, you bring the pistol over to Phil's car, and throw it onto the passenger seat. Looking inside, the car has dice hanging on the mirror, and is filled to the brim with red suits. On the dashboard sits a photo of Phil, his wife, and his three kids, all wearing bright red suits. Phil might've been crazy, but at least he was consistent.

You get in the car, and drive it down the road, before turning into the woods. You drive a mile in, before parking the car before the lake. You get out, and push the car into the water, watching as it submerges.

Whiskers is already awake, sitting perfectly still on the dashboard, silhouetted against the sunrise. She looks regal.
Having Whiskers by your side makes the world a little less cruel.

Not normal static. This static has a rhythm. A pulse. Like breathing.
You reach for the dial to turn it off. The moment your finger touches it, the static stops. Clear silence. Then:
"...eighty-seven... eighty-seven... eighty-seven..."
A voice. Robotic. Monotone. Repeating a number.
Then it changes:
"...fourteen... fourteen... fourteen..."
Then back to static. Then silence. The radio turns itself off.
You sit in your car, hand still on the dial, heart pounding. The numbers echo: 87, 14.
You scribble 87-14 on a receipt. You don't know why. Something tells you they mean something.
The radio stays off for the rest of the night. But the display flickers twice when you're not looking.

You lie there, eyes open, listening to your own breathing and the distant hum of a highway that exists for people going somewhere. Somewhere out there, people are sleeping in actual beds, in actual houses, with mortgages that embarrass them and futures they take for granted.

You wonder if they know. How lucky the ordinary is. How you'd give everything you're chasing just to feel that ordinary again. Probably not. Nobody ever knows until it's already gone and they're lying in a car in the dark making deals with the ceiling.

══════════ ~ ~ ~ Morning, Day 84 ~ ~ ~ ══════════
The sun hits your face through the windshield and you don't even mind. That's how good you feel.

The radio turns on again. 3:17 AM. You weren't sleeping — you never sleep well anymore — so you hear it clearly.
This time, the voice is different. Not robotic. Human. Someone reading from a script.
"Attention. This is a test of the Emergency Broadcast System. This is only a test."
Normal enough. Except it keeps going.
"The person in the car on Route 9 should know that we see them. We see the cards. We see the bets. We see the car with the bad transmission and the dog in the passenger seat."
"This is not a warning. This is a notification. You are being watched. For your own protection."
Click. Static. Silence.
Your hands are white-knuckled on the steering wheel. That broadcast described YOUR life. Your car. Your route. Your dog.
You spin the dial slowly. Station after station of normal radio — pop music, country, a preacher yelling about the end times (less scary than the broadcast). Nothing out of the ordinary.
Until you hit 87.14 FM.
87.14. The numbers from before. 87 and 14.
Dead air. Not static — silence. Like an open microphone in an empty room. You can hear ambient sound: a hum, a clock ticking, someone breathing.
Then: "Good. You found us."
The radio turns itself off.

Blackjack.

You've never felt so rich. So powerful. So fantastic.

You wake up with your fist clenched, as if still holding onto bills that were never there.
The promise of wealth echoes in your mind. What would you sacrifice to feel that way forever?

As my doctor was putting me under, he whispered into my ear: "Let's embark on a journey, a meandering path not unlike the serpentine wanderings of a leaf caught in a capricious autumn breeze, which, as it dances to the silent music of nature, reminds us of the unpredictable choreography of existence. This leaf, let's call it Gerald, flutters with an elegance borne of happenstance, a fragile vessel for the whims of the wind. Gerald's journey is not linear, nor is it bound by the rigid expectations of society's ceaselessly grinding gears. Instead, Gerald twirls, dips, and soars, embracing the chaos with a grace we can only aspire to. Now, consider the ant, industrious and steadfast, a creature of purpose and communal toil. Our ant, whom we'll name Beatrice, marches diligently on her quest for sustenance, her life a testament to the virtues of hard work and persistence. Yet, in the grand tapestry of the cosmos, what is Beatrice but a speck, a mere blip on the infinite canvas of the universe? And yet, does her insignificance in the face of the vast unknown render her efforts moot? I posit that it does not, for in the grand scheme, all actions, large and small, contribute to the intricate mosaic of existence. But back to Gerald, who by now has traversed the convoluted landscapes of our imagination, touching upon the existential questions that haunt the periphery of our consciousness. What can we learn from Gerald and Beatrice? Is it their resilience, their unyielding will to persist in the face of the insurmountable odds stacked against them by the very nature of their existence? Or is it, perhaps, the simple beauty of their dance, a reminder that life, in all its complexity and confusion, offers moments of sublime beauty, fleeting and precious, to be cherished and remembered? As Gerald finally comes to rest upon the earth, joining Beatrice in the eternal cycle of life and death, we are reminded that all journeys, whether they be of leaves or ants or the human heart, are interconnected in the grand, bewildering dance of the cosmos. So, what was the point of this story, you may ask? Well, that, my friend, is entirely up to you."


══════════ ~ ~ ~ Morning, Day 99 ~ ~ ~ ══════════
Your neck doesn't hurt. Your back doesn't hurt. Nothing hurts. Is this a trap?

You've been driving toward the signal. You don't know how you know which direction to go — the radio hums louder when you're heading the right way, softer when you're not.
It leads you off the main road, down a dirt path, past a rusted fence, to a clearing in the woods.
There's a tower. An old radio tower, fifty feet tall, barely standing. The metal is corroded, the guy wires are frayed, and the blinking red light at the top is the only sign it's still active.
At the base of the tower is a small concrete building. The door is steel, rusted, and slightly ajar.
You push the door open. It screams on its hinges.
Inside is a single room. Concrete walls, no windows. A desk with radio equipment — old equipment, vacuum tubes and dials, mixed with modern components that shouldn't be here.
A microphone sits on the desk. Next to it, a logbook.
You open the logbook. Pages and pages of entries. Dates, frequencies, and descriptions of... people. Drivers. Drifters. People on the road.
Your page is near the back. Your car's description. Your daily routine. Your gambling schedule. All documented in meticulous handwriting.
At the bottom of your entry:
"Subject shows resilience. Recommend continued observation. Do not intervene. Let the road decide."
The microphone crackles. A voice — the same voice from the broadcast — fills the room:
"You found the tower. Most people don't get this far. Now the question is: what are you going to do with what you've found?"

Your mind feels... foggy. Something isn't right.
You grab the logbook and run. Behind you, the equipment sparks and hisses. By the time you reach your car, the red light on the tower goes dark.

A hunched figure is walking along the tideline ahead of you, picking things up and putting them in a bucket. An old man, collecting shells.

══════════ ~ ~ ~ Morning, Day 102 ~ ~ ~ ══════════

You don't check your phone. The buzzing stops. The loop... freezes — time itself holding its breath, waiting to see if you'll flinch.

Then everything resumes. You're free, and you remember all three loops with perfect clarity. The memory feels like something you earned.

Why is truth made a mere matter of arithmetic - and only of addition at that? Why is everything twisted out of all sense to fit everything else? There must be some reason. I don't know. A bird is singing outside your car. You don't want to punch it. Progress.

You get cozy in your car, and begin to doze off. That's all for Day 104.
As you sleep, you dream and dream about the sand beneath your feet, the waterfall above you raining water down, splashing in the river, leading out to the ocean and the horizon before you. The sun looks so bright in the fading orange sky, and the hot sand began to cool below you. Before you get the chance to say goodbye, you wake up, having slept through all of Day 105 and Day 106.
As you awake on Day 107, you notice the raindrops begin to slow down, clouds begin to clear, and a golden ray of sunshine fills your soaked wagon. Looking in the seat next to you, your pile of green bills brings a sparkle to your eyes. You hear the money call to you. It's time. Let's go win some hands.
As the sun begins to fall, you collect your money, and leave the safety of your wagon. You barrel out into the damp air, up the muddy dirt road, and into the casino.
